If the maximum force that any member can support is 8 kN
in tension and 6 kN in compression, determine the
maximum force Pthat can be supported at joint D.
60°

A D

P
determining the member forces.

+c©F = 0; F sin 60° - P = 0 F = 1.1547P T
y DC DC 1 2
+
:©F = 0; F - 1.1547Pcos 60° = 0 F = 0.57735P C
x DE DE 1 2
JointC:
+c©F = 0; F sin 60° - 1.1547Psin 60° = 0
y CE
F = 1.1547P C
CE 1 2
+
:©F = 0; 2 1.1547Pcos 60° - F = 0 F = 1.1547P T
x 1 2 CB CB 1 2
JointB:
+c©F = 0; F sin 60° - F sin 60° = 0 F = F = F
y BE BA BE BA
+
:©F = 0; 1.1547P - 2Fcos 60° = 0 F = 1.1547P
x
Thus,
F = 1.1547P C F = 1.1547P T
BE 1 2 BA 1 2

+
:©F = 0; F + 1.1547Pcos 60° - 1.1547Pcos 60°
x EA
-0.57735P = 0
F = 0.57735P C
EA 1 2

member is 1.1547P.For this case,compression controls which requires
1.1547P = 6
P = 5.20kN Ans.

6–25.
Determine the force in each member of the truss in terms of  P P
the external loading and state if the members are in tension
or compression. Take P = 2 kN. 2 m

Solution
Support Reactions. Not required.
Method of Joints: We will start the joint equilibrium analysis at joint C, followed by
joint D and finally joint A.
Joint C. Fig. a
|  +cΣF  | 0; F | sin 60°       | 2 0  |        F | 2.309 kN (C)    | 2.31 kN (C)     Ans. |      |

|  +cΣF = | 0;    | F cos 30° | - F   | sin 30° | - 2 = 0  |     | (2) |
| y       |       | DA        | DB    |         |          |     |     |
Solving Eqs. (1) and (2)
| F = 4.00  kN (T)  |     |     | F = 4.6188  kN (C) |     | = 4.62 kN (C)  |     | Ans. |
| ----------------- | --- | --- | ------------------ | --- | -------------- | --- | ---- |
| DB                |     |     | DA                 |     |                |     |      |

Method of Joints: We will start the joint equilibrium analysis at joint C, followed by
joint D and finally joint A.
Joint C. Fig. a
|  +cΣF | = 0;    |   F  | sin 60°         | - P | = 0    | F = 1.1547P (C) |             |     |

Joint D. Fig. b
| + ΣF  | 0;    |   F | cos 30° | F     | sin 30° | 0.5774P | 0   | (1) |
| ----- | ----- | --- | ------- | ----- | ------- | ------- | --- | --- |
| S     | x =   | DB  |         | - DA  |         | -       | =   |     |
|  +cΣF | = 0;  |   F | cos 30° | - F   | sin 30° | - P =   | 0   | (2) |

|     |     |     | F DA = | 2.3094P (C)  |     |   F DB | = 2.00P (T) |     |

Joint C. Fig. c
| + ΣF  | 0;    |   2.3094 P sin 30° |                    |     | F    | 0    F | 1.1547P (C) |     |
| ----- | ----- | ------------------ | ------------------ | --- | ---- | ------ | ----------- | --- |
| S     | x =   |                    |                    |     | - AB | =      | AB =        |     |
|  +cΣF | = 0;  |   N                | - 2.3094 p cos 30° |     | =    | 0    N | = 2.00P     |     |
|       | y     |                    | A                  |     |      |        | A           |     |
By observation, members DA and DB are subjected to maximum compression and
tension, respectively. Thus, they will reach the limit first.
|     | F DA | = (F | C ) max ;  | 2.3094P | = 3    | P = 1.299 kN | = 1.30 kN (Control!) Ans. |     |

6–67.
Determine the resultant force at pins A, B, and C on the 2 m
three-member frame. 800 N
C
200 N/m
2 m
60(cid:31)
A B
Solution
Free Body Diagram. The frame is being dismembered into members AC and BC of
which their respective FBDs are shown in Fig. a and b.
Equations of Equilibrium. Write the moment equation of equilibrium about point A
for member AC, Fig. a and point B for member BC, Fig. b.
2 2 1
a+ΣM A = 0; C y tan 60° + C x (2) - 200 sin 60° sin 60° = 0 (1)
a+ΣM B = 0; C y (a2) - C x (b2) + 800(2) = 0 a ba b (2)
Solving Eqs. (1) and (2)
C y = -338.12 N C x = 461.88 N
The negative sign indicates that C acts in the sense opposite to that shown in the
y
FBD write the force equation of equilibrium for member AC, Fig. a,
2
S + ΣF x = 0; A x + 200 sin 60° sin 60° - 461.88 = 0 A x = 61.88 N
2
+cΣF y = 0; A y + (-33a8.12) -b200 sin 60° cos 60° = 0 A y = 569.06 N
a b
Also, for member BC, Fig. b
S + ΣF x = 0; B x + 461.88 - 800 = 0 B x = 338.12 N
+cΣF y = 0; -B y - (-338.12) = 0 B y = 338.12 N
Thus,
F C = C x 2 + C y 2 = 461.88 2 + (-338.12)2 = 572.41 N = 572 N Ans.
2 2
F A = A x 2 + A y 2 = 61.882 + 569.062 = 572.41 N = 572 N Ans.
2 2
F B = B x 2 + B y 2 = 338.122 + 338.122 = 478.17 N = 478 N Ans.
2 2
Ans:
F C = 572 N
F A = 572 N
F B = 478 N

6–109.
The spring has an unstretched length of 0.3 m. Determine
the angle u for equilibrium if the uniform bars each have a
C
mass of 20 kg. 2 m
u
k (cid:31) 150 N/m B
u
Solution A
Free Body Diagram. The assembly is being dismembered into members
AB and BC of which their respective FBD are shown in Fig. b and a.
Here, the spring stretches x = 2(2 sin u) - 0.3 = 4 sin u - 0.3. Thus,
F SP = kx = 150 (4 sin u - 0.3) = 600 sin u - 45.
Equations of Equilibrium. Considered the equilibrium of member BC, Fig. a,
a+ΣM C = 0; B y (2 cos u) - B x (2 sin u) - 20(9.81) cos u = 0 (1)
Also, member AB, Fig. b
a+ΣM A = 0; -B y (2 cos u) - B x (2 sin u) - 20(9.81) cos u = 0 (2)
+cΣF y = 0; (600 sin u - 45) -20(9.81) - B y = 0 (3)
Solving Eq. (1) and (2)
9.81 cos u
B y = 0 B x = - sin u
Substitute the result of B y = 0 into Eq. (3)
600 sin u - 45 - 20(9.81) = 0
sin u = 0.402
u = 23.7° Ans.
Ans:
u = 23.7°
